<p><i><b>The
Lord
of
the
Rings:
The
Fellowship
of
the
Ring</b></i>
is
a
2001
<a
href="/wiki/Epic_film?qsrc=3044"
title="Epic
film">epic</a><sup
id="cite_ref-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Fantasy_film?qsrc=3044"
title="Fantasy
film">fantasy
film</a><sup
id="cite_ref-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
directed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Peter_Jackson?qsrc=3044"
title="Peter
Jackson">Peter
Jackson</a>
based
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/The_Fellowship_of_the_Ring?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Fellowship
of
the
Ring">first
volume</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/J._R._R._Tolkien?qsrc=3044"
title="J.
R.
R.
Tolkien">J.
R.
R.
Tolkien</a>'s
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Lord
of
the
Rings">The
Lord
of
the
Rings</a></i>
(1954–1955).
It
was
followed
by
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Two_Towers?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Lord
of
the
Rings:
The
Two
Towers">The
Two
Towers</a></i>
(2002)
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Return_of_the_King?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Lord
of
the
Rings:
The
Return
of
the
King">The
Return
of
the
King</a></i>
(2003),
based
on
the
second
and
third
volumes
of
<i>The
Lord
of
the
Rings</i>.</p>








<p>Set
in
<a
href="/wiki/Middle-earth?qsrc=3044"
title="Middle-earth">Middle-earth</a>,
the
story
tells
of
the
Dark
Lord
<a
href="/wiki/Sauron?qsrc=3044"
title="Sauron">Sauron</a>,
who
is
seeking
the
<a
href="/wiki/One_Ring?qsrc=3044"
title="One
Ring">One
Ring</a>.
The
Ring
has
found
its
way
to
the
young
<a
href="/wiki/Hobbit?qsrc=3044"
title="Hobbit">hobbit</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Frodo_Baggins?qsrc=3044"
title="Frodo
Baggins">Frodo
Baggins</a>
(<a
href="/wiki/Elijah_Wood?qsrc=3044"
title="Elijah
Wood">Elijah
Wood</a>).
The
fate
of
Middle-earth
hangs
in
the
balance
as
Frodo
and
eight
companions
who
form
the
<a
href="/wiki/The_Fellowship_of_the_Ring?qsrc=3044#Members_of_the_Fellowship_of_the_Ring"
title="The
Fellowship
of
the
Ring">Fellowship
of
the
Ring</a>
begin
their
journey
to
<a
href="/wiki/Mount_Doom?qsrc=3044"
title="Mount
Doom">Mount
Doom</a>
in
the
land
of
<a
href="/wiki/Mordor?qsrc=3044"
title="Mordor">Mordor</a>,
the
only
place
where
the
Ring
can
be
destroyed.</p>








<p>Released
on
10
December
2001,
the
film
was
highly
acclaimed
by
critics
and
fans
alike,
especially
as
many
of
the
latter
judged
it
to
be
the
most
sufficiently
faithful
adaptation
of
the
original
story
out
of
Jackson's
<a
href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_film_trilogy?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Lord
of
the
Rings
film
trilogy"
class="mw-redirect">film
trilogy</a>.
It
was
a
major
box
office
success,
earning
over
$870&nbsp;million
worldwide,
and
the
second
highest-grossing
film
of
2001
in
the
U.S.
and
worldwide
(behind
<i><a
href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Philosopher%27s_Stone_(film)?qsrc=3044"
title="Harry
Potter
and
the
Philosopher's
Stone
(film)">Harry
Potter
and
the
Philosopher's
Stone</a></i>)
which
made
it
the
5th
highest-grossing
film
ever
at
the
time.</p>








<p>Today
it
is
the
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films?qsrc=3044"
title="List
of
highest-grossing
films">26th
highest-grossing
worldwide
film</a>
of
all
time.
It
won
four
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_Award?qsrc=3044"
title="Academy
Award">Academy
Awards</a>
and
five
<a
href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Film_and_Television_Arts?qsrc=3044"
title="British
Academy
of
Film
and
Television
Arts">BAFTAs</a>,
including
Best
Film
and
Best
Director
BAFTA
awards.
The
<i>Special
Extended
Edition</i>
was
released
to
DVD
on
12
November
2002
and
to
<a
href="/wiki/Blu-ray?qsrc=3044"
title="Blu-ray"
class="mw-redirect">Blu-ray</a>
on
28
June
2011.
In
2007,
<i>The
Fellowship
of
the
Ring</i>
was
voted
number
50
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/American_Film_Institute?qsrc=3044"
title="American
Film
Institute">American
Film
Institute</a>'s
list
of
<a
href="/wiki/AFI%27s_100_Years...100_Movies_(10th_Anniversary_Edition)?qsrc=3044"
title="AFI's
100
Years...100
Movies
(10th
Anniversary
Edition)">100
greatest
American
films</a>.
The
AFI
also
voted
it
the
second
greatest
fantasy
film
of
all
time
during
their
<a
href="/wiki/AFI%27s_10_Top_10?qsrc=3044"
title="AFI's
10
Top
10">AFI's
10
Top
10</a>
special.</p>

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Plot">Plot</span></h2>








<p>In
the
<a
href="/wiki/Second_Age?qsrc=3044"
title="Second
Age">Second
Age</a>,
the
Dark
Lord
<a
href="/wiki/Sauron?qsrc=3044"
title="Sauron">Sauron</a>
attempts
to
conquer
<a
href="/wiki/Middle-Earth?qsrc=3044"
title="Middle-Earth"
class="mw-redirect">Middle-Earth</a>
using
his
<a
href="/wiki/One_Ring?qsrc=3044"
title="One
Ring">One
Ring</a>.
In
battle
against
the
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_Middle-earth_wars_and_battles?qsrc=3044#War_of_the_Last_Alliance"
title="List
of
Middle-earth
wars
and
battles">Elves
and
Men</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Isildur?qsrc=3044"
title="Isildur">Prince
Isildur</a>
cuts
the
Ring
from
Sauron's
hand,
destroying
his
physical
form
and
vanquishing
his
army.
However,
Sauron's
&quot;life
force&quot;
is
bound
to
the
Ring,
allowing
him
to
survive
while
the
Ring
remains.
Isildur,
corrupted
by
the
Ring's
power,
refuses
to
destroy
it.
When
Isildur
is
killed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Orc_(Middle-earth)?qsrc=3044"
title="Orc
(Middle-earth)">Orcs</a>,
the
Ring
is
lost
in
a
river
for
2,500
years.
The
Ring
is
found
by
<a
href="/wiki/Gollum?qsrc=3044"
title="Gollum">Gollum</a>,
who
possesses
it
for
centuries
until
it
is
found
by
the
<a
href="/wiki/Hobbit?qsrc=3044"
title="Hobbit">Hobbit</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Bilbo_Baggins?qsrc=3044"
title="Bilbo
Baggins">Bilbo
Baggins</a>.</p>








<p>Sixty
years
later,
Bilbo
leaves
the
Ring
to
his
nephew,
<a
href="/wiki/Frodo_Baggins?qsrc=3044"
title="Frodo
Baggins">Frodo
Baggins</a>.
Upon
learning
that
the
Ring
belonged
to
Sauron,
the
<a
href="/wiki/Wizard_(Middle-earth)?qsrc=3044"
title="Wizard
(Middle-earth)">Wizard</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Gandalf?qsrc=3044"
title="Gandalf">Gandalf
the
Grey</a>
warns
Frodo
that
Sauron's
forces
will
come
for
him.
Gandalf
catches
Frodo's
gardener
<a
href="/wiki/Samwise_Gamgee?qsrc=3044"
title="Samwise
Gamgee">Samwise
Gamgee</a>
&quot;eavesdropping&quot;
underneath
a
window
and
sends
him
with
Frodo
to
leave
the
Shire.
Gandalf
rides
to
<a
href="/wiki/Isengard?qsrc=3044"
title="Isengard">Isengard</a>
to
meet
with
the
head
of
his
order,
<a
href="/wiki/Saruman?qsrc=3044"
title="Saruman">Saruman
the
White</a>,
who
reveals
that
Sauron's
servants,
the
<a
href="/wiki/Nazg%C3%BBl?qsrc=3044"
title="Nazg&ucirc;l">Nazg&ucirc;l</a>,
have
been
sent
to
capture
the
Ring.
Saruman
reveals
himself
to
be
in
service
to
Sauron,
and
imprisons
Gandalf
atop
his
tower.
Saruman
commands
Sauron's
Orcs
to
construct
weapons
of
war
and
produce
a
new
breed
of
Orc
fighters:
the
<a
href="/wiki/Uruk-hai?qsrc=3044"
title="Uruk-hai">Uruk-hai</a>.</p>








<p>While
traveling
to
<a
href="/wiki/Bree_(Middle-earth)?qsrc=3044"
title="Bree
(Middle-earth)">Bree</a>,
Frodo
and
Sam
are
joined
by
<a
href="/wiki/Meriadoc_Brandybuck?qsrc=3044"
title="Meriadoc
Brandybuck">Merry</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Peregrin_Took?qsrc=3044"
title="Peregrin
Took">Pippin</a>,
and
are
nearly
captured
by
the
Nazg&ucirc;l.
At
the
<a
href="/wiki/Inn_of_the_Prancing_Pony?qsrc=3044"
title="Inn
of
the
Prancing
Pony"
class="mw-redirect">Inn
of
the
Prancing
Pony</a>,
Frodo
meets
the
mysterious
<a
href="/wiki/Ranger_(Middle-earth)?qsrc=3044"
title="Ranger
(Middle-earth)">ranger</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Aragorn?qsrc=3044"
title="Aragorn">Aragorn</a>,
who
hides
them
from
their
pursuers
and
agrees
to
lead
them
to
<a
href="/wiki/Rivendell?qsrc=3044"
title="Rivendell">Rivendell</a>.
During
the
journey
they
are
attacked
by
the
Nazg&ucirc;l.
Aragorn
fights
off
the
creatures,
but
Frodo
is
wounded
by
their
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_Middle-earth_weapons_and_armour?qsrc=3044#Morgul-blade"
title="List
of
Middle-earth
weapons
and
armour">morgul
blade</a>,
which
will
turn
him
into
a
wraith.
While
chased
by
the
Nazg&ucirc;l,
Frodo
is
saved
by
the
<a
href="/wiki/Elf_(Middle-earth)?qsrc=3044"
title="Elf
(Middle-earth)">Elf</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Arwen?qsrc=3044"
title="Arwen">Arwen</a>
who
uses
her
magic
to
summon
a
surge
of
water
that
sweeps
away
the
pursuing
Nazg&ucirc;l.
Arwen
takes
Frodo
to
Rivendell
where
he
is
healed
by
her
father,
<a
href="/wiki/Elrond?qsrc=3044"
title="Elrond">Elrond</a>.
Gandalf
escapes
Saruman's
tower
with
the
aid
of
Gwaihir
the
<a
href="/wiki/Eagle_(Middle-earth)?qsrc=3044"
title="Eagle
(Middle-earth)">eagle</a>
and
travels
to
Rivendell.
Elrond
calls
a
<a
href="/wiki/The_Fellowship_of_the_Ring?qsrc=3044#Book_II:_The_Fellowship_of_the_Ring"
title="The
Fellowship
of
the
Ring">council</a>
of
the
races
still
loyal
to
Middle-earth
to
decide
what
should
be
done
with
the
Ring.
It
is
revealed
that
the
Ring
can
only
be
destroyed
by
throwing
it
into
the
fires
of
<a
href="/wiki/Mount_Doom?qsrc=3044"
title="Mount
Doom">Mount
Doom</a>,
where
it
was
forged.
Frodo
volunteers
to
take
the
Ring,
accompanied
by
Sam,
Merry,
Pippin,
Gandalf,
and
Aragorn.
They
are
joined
by
the
Elf
<a
href="/wiki/Legolas?qsrc=3044"
title="Legolas">Legolas</a>,
the
<a
href="/wiki/Dwarf_(Middle-earth)?qsrc=3044"
title="Dwarf
(Middle-earth)">Dwarf</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Gimli_(Middle-earth)?qsrc=3044"
title="Gimli
(Middle-earth)">Gimli</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Boromir?qsrc=3044"
title="Boromir">Boromir</a>,
man
of
<a
href="/wiki/Gondor?qsrc=3044"
title="Gondor">Gondor</a>,
to
form
the
<a
href="/wiki/The_Fellowship_of_the_Ring?qsrc=3044#Members_of_the_Fellowship_of_the_Ring"
title="The
Fellowship
of
the
Ring">Fellowship
of
the
Ring</a>.</p>








<p>The
Fellowship
set
out
but
are
hindered
by
Saruman's
magic.
They
travel
through
the
dwarf
<a
href="/wiki/Moria_(Middle-earth)?qsrc=3044"
title="Moria
(Middle-earth)">Mines
of
Moria</a>.
Inside,
they
find
that
Orcs
have
overrun
the
mines
and
slain
the
Dwarves;
they
also
realize
that
Gollum
is
following
them,
determined
to
reclaim
the
Ring.
The
Fellowship
is
attacked
by
Orcs
and
a
<a
href="/wiki/Balrog?qsrc=3044"
title="Balrog">Balrog</a>,
an
ancient
<a
href="/wiki/Demon?qsrc=3044"
title="Demon">demon</a>
of
fire
and
shadow.
Gandalf
confronts
the
Balrog,
allowing
the
others
to
escape,
but
both
Gandalf
and
the
Balrog
fall
into
an
abyss.
Mourning
Gandalf's
apparent
death,
the
group
flees
to
<a
href="/wiki/Lothl%C3%B3rien?qsrc=3044"
title="Lothl&oacute;rien">Lothl&oacute;rien</a>,
where
they
are
sheltered
by
its
rulers,
the
Elves
<a
href="/wiki/Galadriel?qsrc=3044"
title="Galadriel">Galadriel</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Celeborn?qsrc=3044"
title="Celeborn">Celeborn</a>.
That
night,
Galadriel
informs
Frodo
that
it
is
his
destiny
to
destroy
the
Ring.
The
Fellowship
continue
their
journey.
Meanwhile,
Saruman
assembles
a
force
of
Uruk-hai
to
hunt
the
Fellowship.</p>








<p>After
arriving
at
Parth
Galen,
Boromir
gives
in
to
the
Ring's
corruption
and
tries
to
take
it
from
Frodo,
believing
that
it
is
the
only
way
to
save
his
realm.
Frodo
manages
to
escape
by
wearing
the
Ring
and
becoming
invisible.
Boromir
realizes
what
he
has
done,
and
attempts
to
find
Frodo,
who
decides
to
continue
his
journey
alone,
heeding
Galadriel's
warning
that
the
Ring
will
eventually
corrupt
the
other
members
of
the
Fellowship.
The
Uruk-hai
arrive
and
Aragorn,
Legolas,
and
Gimli
attempt
to
hold
them
off
while
Frodo
escapes.
Merry
and
Pippin
lead
the
Orcs
away
from
Frodo
and
are
nearly
killed.
Boromir
tries
to
save
them,
but
in
the
process
is
shot
fatally
by
the
Uruk-Hai
leader,
Lurtz.
The
Uruk-Hai
capture
Merry
and
Pippin.
Aragorn
slays
Lurtz
and
tends
to
a
dying
Boromir,
and
promises
him
that
the
world
of
men
will
not
fall.
Boromir
dies
with
Aragorn,
Gimli
and
Legolas
by
his
side.</p>








<p>Sam
finds
Frodo,
who
reluctantly
lets
Sam
join
him.
Aragorn,
Legolas
and
Gimli
set
out
to
rescue
Merry
and
Pippin.
As
Frodo
and
Sam
gaze
out
at
the
land
before
them,
they
grieve
over
the
others.
Frodo
says
that
he
is
glad
that
Sam
is
with
him
and
the
two
Hobbits
set
off
towards
Mordor.</p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Cast">Cast</span></h2>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:302px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Fellowship.JPG"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com:80/ts?u=/wikipedia/en/4/40/Fellowship.JPG"
width="300"
height="136"
class="thumbimage"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Fellowship.JPG"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="/images/wikipedia/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
The
eponymous
Fellowship
from
left
to
right:
(Top
row)
Aragorn,
Gandalf,
Legolas,
Boromir,
(bottom
row)
Sam,
Frodo,
Merry,
Pippin,
Gimli.









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Before
filming
began
on
11
October
1999,
the
principal
actors
trained
for
six
weeks
in
sword
fighting
(with
<a
href="/wiki/Bob_Anderson_(fencer)?qsrc=3044"
title="Bob
Anderson
(fencer)">Bob
Anderson</a>),
riding
and
boating.
Jackson
hoped
such
activities
would
allow
the
cast
to
bond
so
chemistry
would
be
evident
on
screen
as
well
as
getting
them
used
to
life
in
<a
href="/wiki/Wellington?qsrc=3044"
title="Wellington">Wellington</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-cast_4-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cast-4"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
They
were
also
trained
to
pronounce
Tolkien's
verses
properly.<sup
id="cite_ref-officialguide_5-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-officialguide-5"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
the
shoot,
the
nine
cast
members
playing
the
Fellowship
got
a
tattoo,
the
Elvish
symbol
for
the
number
nine,
with
the
exception
of
<a
href="/wiki/John_Rhys-Davies?qsrc=3044"
title="John
Rhys-Davies">John
Rhys-Davies</a>,
whose
stunt
double
got
the
tattoo
instead.<sup
id="cite_ref-master_6-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-master-6"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
film
is
noted
for
having
an
<a
href="/wiki/Ensemble_cast?qsrc=3044"
title="Ensemble
cast">ensemble
cast</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
some
of
the
cast
and
their
respective
characters
include:</p>








<ul>









<li><a
href="/wiki/Elijah_Wood?qsrc=3044"
title="Elijah
Wood">Elijah
Wood</a>
as
<a
href="/wiki/Frodo_Baggins?qsrc=3044"
title="Frodo
Baggins">Frodo
Baggins</a>:
A
<a
href="/wiki/Hobbit?qsrc=3044"
title="Hobbit">hobbit</a>
who
inherits
the
<a
href="/wiki/One_Ring?qsrc=3044"
title="One
Ring">One
Ring</a>
from
his
uncle,
Bilbo
Baggins.
He
is
accompanied
on
his
quest
by
his
best
friend
and
fellow
hobbit,
Samwise
Gamgee.
<a
href="/wiki/Elijah_Wood?qsrc=3044"
title="Elijah
Wood">Elijah
Wood</a>
was
the
first
actor
to
be
cast
on
7
July
1999.<sup
id="cite_ref-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
Wood
was
a
fan
of
the
book,
and
he
sent
in
an
audition
dressed
as
Frodo,
reading
lines
from
the
novel.<sup
id="cite_ref-circus_9-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-circus-9"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
Wood
was
selected
from
150
actors
who
auditioned.<sup
id="cite_ref-bumps_10-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bumps-10"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></li>









<li><a
href="/wiki/Ian_McKellen?qsrc=3044"
title="Ian
McKellen">Ian
McKellen</a>
as
<a
href="/wiki/Gandalf?qsrc=3044"
title="Gandalf">Gandalf
the
Grey</a>:
An
<a
href="/wiki/Wizard_(Middle-earth)?qsrc=3044"
title="Wizard
(Middle-earth)">Istari
wizard</a>
and
mentor
to
Frodo,
who
helps
him
decide
what
to
do
with
the
Ring.
He
becomes
the
leader
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/The_Fellowship_of_the_Ring?qsrc=3044#Members_of_the_Fellowship_of_the_Ring"
title="The
Fellowship
of
the
Ring">Fellowship</a>
after
it
is
decided
to
take
the
Ring
to
<a
href="/wiki/Mount_Doom?qsrc=3044"
title="Mount
Doom">Mount
Doom</a>
and
destroy
it.
<a
href="/wiki/Sean_Connery?qsrc=3044"
title="Sean
Connery">Sean
Connery</a>
was
approached
for
the
role,
but
did
not
understand
the
plot,<sup
id="cite_ref-circus_9-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-circus-9"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
while
<a
href="/wiki/Patrick_Stewart?qsrc=3044"
title="Patrick
Stewart">Patrick
Stewart</a>
turned
it
down,
as
he
disliked
the
script.<sup
id="cite_ref-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
Before
being
cast,
McKellen
had
to
sort
his
schedule
with
<a
href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox?qsrc=3044"
title="20th
Century
Fox">20th
Century
Fox</a>
as
there
was
a
two-month
overlap
with
<i><a
href="/wiki/X-Men_(film)?qsrc=3044"
title="X-Men
(film)">X-Men</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-bumps_10-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bumps-10"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
enjoyed
playing
Gandalf
the
Grey
more
than
his
transformed
state
in
the
next
two
films,<sup
id="cite_ref-master_6-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-master-6"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
based
his
accent
on
Tolkien.
Unlike
his
on-screen
character,
McKellen
did
not
spend
much
time
with
the
actors
playing
the
Hobbits,
instead
working
with
their
scale
doubles.<sup
id="cite_ref-cast_4-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cast-4"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></li>









<li><a
href="/wiki/Sean_Astin?qsrc=3044"
title="Sean
Astin">Sean
Astin</a>
as
<a
href="/wiki/Samwise_Gamgee?qsrc=3044"
title="Samwise
Gamgee">Samwise
&quot;Sam&quot;
Gamgee</a>:
A
Hobbit
gardener
and
Frodo's
best
friend.
When
caught
eavesdropping,
Sam
is
made
to
become
Frodo's
companion
and
from
then
on
becomes
very
loyal.
Astin,
who
had
recently

a

with
the
18-year-old
Wood
in
a

manner,
which
mirrored
Sam's
relationship
with
Frodo.<sup
id="cite_ref-cast_4-2"
class="reference"><a

<li><a

<a

Dubbed
Strider,

is
a
<a
href="/wiki/D%C3%BAnedain?qsrc=3044"

<a

(Middle-earth)">ranger</a>
and
the
heir
to
the

of
<a

He
travels
with

Fellowship
on
their
journey
to
<a
href="/wiki/Mordor?qsrc=3044"
title="Mordor">Mordor</a>.
He
is
unsure
of
whether
to
become
King
following
the
failure
of
his
ancestor,
<a
href="/wiki/Isildur?qsrc=3044"

to

href="/wiki/Daniel_Day-Lewis?qsrc=3044"
title="Daniel
Day-Lewis">Daniel
Day-Lewis</a>

at

<a

title="Nicolas
Cage">Nicolas

because

&quot;family

<a

title="Vin

Diesel</a>,

<a
href="/wiki/Stuart_Townsend?qsrc=3044"

in

before
being

during

when
Jackson
realised
he
was
too
young.<sup
id="cite_ref-circus_9-2"

<a
href="/wiki/Russell_Crowe?qsrc=3044"
title="Russell
Crowe">Russell
Crowe</a>
was
considered
as
a
replacement,
but
he
turned
it
down
after
taking
what

thought
to
be
a
similar

in
<i><a
href="/wiki/Gladiator_(2000_film)?qsrc=3044"
title="Gladiator
(2000
film)">Gladiator</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-circus_9-3"
class="reference"><a

Day-Lewis
was

but

again.<sup
id="cite_ref-DDL_12-1"

Mark
Ordesky
saw

in
a
play.
Mortensen's

of

to

id="cite_ref-cast_4-3"

on

a

from

Anderson
and

on
Weathertop.<sup
id="cite_ref-filming_14-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-filming-14"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
Mortensen
became
a
hit
with

crew
by
patching
up
his
costume<sup
id="cite_ref-costumes_15-0"

<li><a

<li><a

<a
href="/wiki/Galadriel?qsrc=3044"

An
Elf
and

href="/wiki/Lothl%C3%B3rien?qsrc=3044"

her
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_Middle-earth_objects?qsrc=3044#Mirror_of_Galadriel"
title="List
of
Middle-earth
objects">mirror</a>
and
gives
him
the
Light
of
<a
href="/wiki/E%C3%A4rendil?qsrc=3044"
title="E&auml;rendil">E&auml;rendil</a>.
<a
href="/wiki/Tilda_Swinton?qsrc=3044"
title="Tilda
Swinton">Tilda
Swinton</a>
was
also
a
possibility
to
the
role,
but
she
turned
it
down,
since
she
was
going
to
play
a
similar
role
as
Jadis,
the
<a
href="/wiki/White_Witch?qsrc=3044"
title="White
Witch">White
Witch</a>
in
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Chronicles_of_Narnia:_The_Lion,_the_Witch_and_the_Wardrobe?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Chronicles
of
Narnia:
The
Lion,
the
Witch
and
the
Wardrobe">The
Chronicles
of
Narnia:
The
Lion,
the
Witch
and
the
Wardrobe</a></i>.</li>









<li><a
href="/wiki/Liv_Tyler?qsrc=3044"
title="Liv
Tyler">Liv
Tyler</a>
as
<a
href="/wiki/Arwen?qsrc=3044"
title="Arwen">Arwen</a>:
An
elf,
Arwen
escorts
Frodo
to
Rivendell
after
he
is
stabbed
by
the
<a
href="/wiki/Witch-king_of_Angmar?qsrc=3044"
title="Witch-king
of
Angmar">Witch-king</a>.
She
is
the
daughter
of
Elrond,
and
Aragorn's
lover
to
whom
she
gives
the
<a
href="/wiki/Arwen?qsrc=3044#Adaptations"
title="Arwen">Evenstar</a>
necklace.
The
filmmakers
approached
Tyler
after
seeing
her
performance
in
<i><a
href="/wiki/Plunkett_%26_Macleane?qsrc=3044"
title="Plunkett
&amp;
Macleane">Plunkett
&amp;
Macleane</a></i>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/New_Line_Cinema?qsrc=3044"
title="New
Line
Cinema">New
Line
Cinema</a>
leaped
at
the
opportunity
of
having
one
Hollywood
star
in
the
film.
Actress
<a
href="/wiki/Helena_Bonham_Carter?qsrc=3044"
title="Helena
Bonham
Carter">Helena
Bonham
Carter</a>
had
expressed
interest
in
the
role.<sup
id="cite_ref-circus_9-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-circus-9"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
Tyler
came
to
shoot
on
short
occasions,
and
bonded
most
with
Bloom.<sup
id="cite_ref-cast_4-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cast-4"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
was
one
of
the
last
actors
to
be
cast,
on
25
August
1999.<sup
id="cite_ref-16"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></li>









<li><a
href="/wiki/Ian_Holm?qsrc=3044"
title="Ian
Holm">Ian
Holm</a>
as
<a
href="/wiki/Bilbo_Baggins?qsrc=3044"
title="Bilbo
Baggins">Bilbo
Baggins</a>:
Frodo's
uncle
who
gives
him
the
Ring
after
he
decides
to
retire
to
Rivendell.
At
Rivendell,
he
gives
Frodo
a
<i><a
href="/wiki/Mithril?qsrc=3044"
title="Mithril">mithril</a></i>
mail-shirt
and
his
own
sword,
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_Middle-earth_weapons_and_armour?qsrc=3044#Sting"
title="List
of
Middle-earth
weapons
and
armour">Sting</a>,
which
can
detect
the
presence
of
nearby
orcs
by
emitting
a
bluish
glow.
Holm
previously
played
Frodo
in
a
<a
href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(1981_radio_series)?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Lord
of
the
Rings
(1981
radio
series)">1981
radio
adaption
of
<i>The
Lord
of
the
Rings</i></a>,
and
was
cast
as
Bilbo
after
Jackson
remembered
his
performance.<sup
id="cite_ref-circus_9-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-circus-9"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Sylvester_McCoy?qsrc=3044"
title="Sylvester
McCoy">Sylvester
McCoy</a>
was
contacted
about
playing
the
role,
and
was
kept
in
place
as
a
potential
Bilbo
for
six
months
before
Jackson
went
with
Holm.<sup
id="cite_ref-17"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></li>









<li><a
href="/wiki/Lawrence_Makoare?qsrc=3044"

Makoare</a>
as

of

The

of
Saruman's
orc
forces

hunt

guarding

Lothl&oacute;rien.</li>









<li><a

An
Elven-King
and
last
ruler
of
<a

fought
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_Middle-earth_wars_and_battles?qsrc=3044#War_of_the_Last_Alliance"

of
Middle-earth
wars
and
battles">War
of
the
Last
Alliance</a>.</li>

by

Son
of

of

who
fought
in

War
Of

Alliance.

ambushed
by

Orcs
when
The
<a

Ring">One
Ring</a>
is
passed
onto
him
after
he
cut
off
Sauron's
hand

<a

of

and

during
the
war.</li>








</ul>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Comparison_with_the_source_material">Comparison
with
the
source
material</span></h2>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:142px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Unico_Anello.png"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com:80/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Unico_Anello.png/140px-Unico_Anello.png"
width="140"
height="121"
class="thumbimage"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Unico_Anello.png"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="/images/wikipedia/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
Image
showing
the
inscriptions
on
the
Ring.









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Jackson,
Walsh
and
Boyens
made
numerous
changes
to
the
story,
for
purposes
of
pacing
and
character
development.
Jackson
said
his
main
desire
was
to
make
a
film
focused
primarily
on
Frodo
and
the
Ring,
the
&quot;backbone&quot;
of
the
story.<sup
id="cite_ref-Story_18-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Story-18"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
prologue
condenses
Tolkien's
backstory,
in
which
The
Last
Alliance's
seven
year
siege
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Barad-d%C3%BBr?qsrc=3044"
title="Barad-d&ucirc;r">Barad-d&ucirc;r</a>
is
a
single
battle,
where
Sauron
is
shown
to
explode,
though
Tolkien
only
said
his
spirit
flees.<sup
id="cite_ref-Letters_19-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Letters-19"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Events
at
the
beginning
of
the
film
are
condensed
or
omitted
altogether.
In
the
book
the
time
between
Gandalf
leaving
the
Ring
to
Frodo
and
returning
to
reveal
its
inscription,
which
is
17
years,
is
compressed
for
timing
reasons.<sup
id="cite_ref-DirectorCommentary_20-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-DirectorCommentary-20"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup>
Frodo
also
spends
a
few
months
preparing
to
move
to
Buckland,
on
the
eastern
border
of
the
shire.
This
move
is
omitted
and
combined
with
him
setting
out
for
Rivendell.
Also
compressed
is
the
time
between
Frodo
and
Sam
leaving
Bag
End
and
their
meeting
Merry
and
Pippin.
Characters
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Bombadil?qsrc=3044"
title="Tom
Bombadil">Tom
Bombadil</a>
are
left
out
to
simplify
the
plot
and
increase
the
threat
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Nazg%C3%BBl?qsrc=3044"
title="Nazg&ucirc;l">Ringwraiths</a>.
Such
sequences
are
left
out
to
make
time
to
introduce
Saruman,
who
in
the
book
doesn't
appear
until
a
flashback
told
at
the
Council
of
Elrond.
Saruman's
role
is
enhanced:
he
is
to
blame
for
the
blizzard
on
Caradhras,
a
role
taken
from
Sauron
and/or
Caradhras
itself
in
the
book.
Gandalf's
capture
by
Saruman
is
also
expanded
with
a
fight
sequence.</p>








<p>The
role
of
<a
href="/wiki/Barliman_Butterbur?qsrc=3044"
title="Barliman
Butterbur">Barliman
Butterbur</a>
at
the
Prancing
Pony
is
largely
removed
for
time
and
dramatic
flow.</p>








<p>The
events
at
Weathertop
were
also
altered.
The
location
of
the
fight
against
the
Ringwraiths
was
changed
to
the
ruins
on
top
of
the
hill
rather
than
a
campsite
at
its
base.
When
Frodo
was
stabbed
in
the
book,
the
party
spent
two
weeks
travelling
to
Rivendell,
but
in
the
film
this
is
shortened
to
less
than
a
week,
with
Frodo's
condition
worsening
at
a
commensurately
greater
rate.
<a
href="/wiki/Arwen?qsrc=3044"
title="Arwen">Arwen</a>
was
given
a
greater
role
in
the
film,
accompanying
Frodo
all
the
way
to
Rivendell,
while
in
the
book
Frodo
faced
the
Ringwraiths
alone
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_Middle-earth_rivers?qsrc=3044#Bruinen"
title="List
of
Middle-earth
rivers">Ford
of
Bruinen</a>.
The
character
of
<a
href="/wiki/Glorfindel?qsrc=3044"
title="Glorfindel">Glorfindel</a>
was
omitted
entirely
and
his
scenes
were
also
given
to
Arwen.
She
was
tacitly
credited
with
the
river
rising
against
the
Ringwraiths,
which
was
the
work
of
her
father
<a
href="/wiki/Elrond?qsrc=3044"
title="Elrond">Elrond</a>
with
aid
from
<a
href="/wiki/Gandalf?qsrc=3044"
title="Gandalf">Gandalf</a>
in
the
book.</p>








<p>A
significant
new
addition
is
Aragorn's
self-doubt,
which
causes
him
to
hesitate
to
claim
the
kingship
of
Gondor.
This
element
is
not
present
in
the
book,
where
Aragorn
intends
to
claim
the
throne
at
an
appropriate
time.
In
the
book
Narsil
is
reforged
immediately
when
he
joins
the
Fellowship,
but
this
event
is
held
over
until
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Return_of_the_King?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Lord
of
the
Rings:
The
Return
of
the
King">Return
of
the
King</a></i>
in
film
to
symbolically
coincide
with
his
acceptance
of
his
title.
These
elements
were
added
because
Peter
Jackson
believed
that
each
character
should
be
forced
to
grow
or
change
over
the
course
of
the
story.</p>








<p><a
href="/wiki/Elrond?qsrc=3044"
title="Elrond">Elrond</a>'s
character
gained
an
adversarial
edge;
he
expresses
doubts
in
the
strength
of
Men
to
resist
Sauron's
evil
after
Isildur's
failure
to
destroy
the
ring
as
depicted
in
the
prologue.
Jackson
also
shortens
the
Council
of
Elrond
by
spreading
its
exposition
into
earlier
parts
of
the
film.
Elrond's
counsellor,
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_Middle-earth_Elves?qsrc=3044#Erestor"
title="List
of
Middle-earth
Elves">Erestor</a>—who
suggested
the
Ring
be
given
to
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Bombadil?qsrc=3044"
title="Tom
Bombadil">Tom
Bombadil</a>—was
completely
absent
from
this
scene.
Gimli's
father,
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_Middle-earth_Dwarves?qsrc=3044#Gl.C3.B3in.2C_son_of_Gr.C3.B3in"
title="List
of
Middle-earth
Dwarves">Gl&oacute;in</a>,
was
also
deemed
unnecessary.</p>








<p>The
tone
of
the
Moria
sequence
was
altered.
Although
in
the
book
the
Fellowship
only
realises
the
Dwarves
are
all
dead
once
they
reach
<a
href="/wiki/Balin_(Middle-earth)?qsrc=3044"
title="Balin
(Middle-earth)">Balin</a>'s
tomb,
the
filmmakers
chose
to
use
<a
href="/wiki/Foreshadowing?qsrc=3044"
title="Foreshadowing">foreshadowing</a>
devices
instead.
Gandalf
says
to
Gimli
he
would
prefer
not
to
enter
Moria,
and
Saruman
is
shown
to
be
aware
of
Gandalf's
reticence,
and
also
reveals
an
illustration
of
the
Balrog
in
one
of
his
books.
The
corpses
of
the
dwarves
are
instantly
shown
as
the
Fellowship
enter
Moria.<sup
id="cite_ref-21"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
terms
of
dramatic
structure,
the
book
simply
ends;
there
is
no
climax,
because
Tolkien
wrote
the
&quot;trilogy&quot;
as
a
single
story
published
in
three
volumes.
Jackson's
version
incorporates
the
first
chapter
of
'&quot;The
Two
Towers&quot;
and
makes
its
events,
told
in
real
time
instead
of
flashback,
simultaneous
with
the
Breaking
of
the
Fellowship.
This
finale
is
played
as
a
climactic
battle,
into
which
he
introduces
the
Uruk-hai
referred
to
as
Lurtz
in
the
script.
In
the
book,
Boromir
is
unable
to
tell
Aragorn
which
hobbits
were
kidnapped
by
the
orcs
before
he
dies.
From
there,
Aragorn
deduces
Frodo's
intentions
when
he
notices
that
a
boat
is
missing
and
Sam's
pack
is
gone.
In
the
film,
Aragorn
and
Frodo
have
a
scene
together
in
which
Frodo's
intentions
are
explicitly
stated.</p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Production">Production</span></h2>








<p>Jackson
began
working
with
<a
href="/wiki/Christian_Rivers?qsrc=3044"
title="Christian
Rivers">Christian
Rivers</a>
to
storyboard
the
trilogy
in
August
1997,
as
well
as
getting
<a
href="/wiki/Richard_Taylor_(filmmaker)?qsrc=3044"
title="Richard
Taylor
(filmmaker)">Richard
Taylor</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Weta_Workshop?qsrc=3044"
title="Weta
Workshop">Weta
Workshop</a>
to
begin
creating
his
interpretation
of
Middle-earth.<sup
id="cite_ref-22"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
Jackson
told
them
to
make
Middle-earth
as
plausible
and
believable
as
possible,
to
think
of
Middle-earth
in
a
historical
manner.<sup
id="cite_ref-Design_23-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Design-23"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
November,<sup
id="cite_ref-Design_23-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Design-23"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Alan_Lee_(illustrator)?qsrc=3044"
title="Alan
Lee
(illustrator)">Alan
Lee</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/John_Howe_(illustrator)?qsrc=3044"
title="John
Howe
(illustrator)">John
Howe</a>
became
the
primary
conceptual
designers
for
the
film
trilogy,
having
had
previous
experience
as
illustrators
for
the
book
and
various
other
tie-ins.
Lee
worked
for
the
Art
Department
creating
places
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Rivendell?qsrc=3044"
title="Rivendell">Rivendell</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Isengard?qsrc=3044"
title="Isengard">Isengard</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Moria_(Middle-earth)?qsrc=3044"
title="Moria
(Middle-earth)">Moria</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Lothl%C3%B3rien?qsrc=3044"
title="Lothl&oacute;rien">Lothl&oacute;rien</a>,
giving
<a
href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau?qsrc=3044"
title="Art
Nouveau">art
nouveau</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Geometry?qsrc=3044"
title="Geometry">geometry</a>
influences
to
the
Elves
and
Dwarves
respectively.<sup
id="cite_ref-Design_23-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Design-23"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-bigature_24-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bigature-24"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup>
Though
Howe
contributed
with
Bag
End
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Minor_places_in_Middle-earth?qsrc=3044#Argonath"
title="Minor
places
in
Middle-earth">Argonath</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-Design_23-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Design-23"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-bigature_24-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bigature-24"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup>
he
focused
working
on
armour
having
studied
it
all
his
life.<sup
id="cite_ref-25"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
Weta
and
the
Art
Department
continued
to
design,
with
Grant
Major
turning
the
Art
Department's
designs
into
architecture,
and
Dan
Hennah
scouting
locations.<sup
id="cite_ref-Design_23-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Design-23"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
1
April
1999,
<a
href="/wiki/Ngila_Dickson?qsrc=3044"
title="Ngila
Dickson">Ngila
Dickson</a>
joined
the
crew
as
costume
designer.
She
and
40
seamstresses
would
create
19,000
costumes,
40
per
version
for
the
actor
and
their
doubles,
ageing
and
wearing
them
out
for
impression
of
age.<sup
id="cite_ref-costumes_15-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-costumes-15"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Special_effects">Special
effects</span></h3>








<p><i>The
Fellowship
of
the
Ring</i>
makes
extensive
use
of
digital,
practical
and
make-up
special
effects
throughout.
One
noticeable
illusion
that
appears
in
almost
every
scene
involves
setting
a
proper
scale
so
that
the
characters
are
all
the
correct
height.
Elijah
Wood,
who
plays
Frodo,
is
5&nbsp;ft
6in
(1.68&nbsp;m)
tall
in
real
life,
but
the
character
of
Frodo
Baggins
is
barely
four
feet
in
height.
Many
different
tricks
were
used
to
depict
the
hobbits
(and
Gimli
the
Dwarf)
as
being
of
diminutive
stature.
(In
a
happy
coincidence,
John-Rhys
Davies&nbsp;—
who
played
Gimli&nbsp;—
is
as
tall
compared
to
the
Hobbit
actors
as
his
character
needed
to
be
compared
to
theirs,
so
he
did
not
need
to
be
filmed
separately
as
a
third
variation
of
height,
and
is
quite
taller
than
Orlando
Bloom,
who
played
Legolas.)
Large
and
small
scale
doubles
were
used
in
certain
scenes,
while
entire
duplicates
of
certain
sets
(including
<a
href="/wiki/Shire_(Middle-earth)?qsrc=3044#Westfarthing"
title="Shire
(Middle-earth)">Bag
End</a>
in
Hobbiton)
were
built
at
two
different
scales,
so
that
the
characters
would
appear
to
be
the
appropriate
size.
At
one
point
in
the
film,
Frodo
runs
along
a
corridor
in
Bag
End,
followed
by
Gandalf.
Elijah
Wood
and
Ian
McKellen
were
filmed
in
separate
versions
of
the
same
corridor,
built
at
two
different
scales,
and
a
fast
camera
pan
conceals
the
edit
between
the
two.
<a
href="/wiki/Forced_perspective?qsrc=3044"
title="Forced
perspective">Forced
perspective</a>
was
also
employed,
so
that
it
would
look
as
though
the
short
Hobbits
were
interacting
with
taller
<a
href="/wiki/Man_(Middle-earth)?qsrc=3044"
title="Man
(Middle-earth)">Men</a>
and
Elves.
Even
the
simple
use
of
kneeling
down,
to
the
filmmakers'
surprise,
turned
out
to
be
an
effective
method
in
creating
the
illusion.</p>








<p>For
the
battle
between
the
Last
Alliance
and
the
forces
of
Sauron
that
begins
the
film,
an
elaborate
<a
href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery?qsrc=3044"
title="Computer-generated
imagery">CGI</a>
animation
system,
called
<a
href="/wiki/MASSIVE_(software)?qsrc=3044"
title="MASSIVE
(software)">MASSIVE</a>,
was
developed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Stephen_Regelous?qsrc=3044"
title="Stephen
Regelous">Stephen
Regelous</a>;
it
allowed
thousands
of
individual
animated
&quot;characters&quot;
in
the
program
to
act
independently.
This
helped
give
the
illusion
of
realism
to
the
battle
sequences.
The
&quot;Making
of&quot;
Lord
of
the
Rings
DVD
reports
some
interesting
initial
problems:
in
the
first
execution
of
a
battle
between
groups
of
characters,
the
wrong
groups
attacked
each
other.
In
another
early
demo,
some
of
the
warriors
at
the
edge
of
the
field
could
be
seen
running
away.
They
were
initially
moving
in
the
wrong
direction,
and
had
been
programmed
to
keep
running
until
they
encountered
an
enemy.</p>








<p>The
digital
creatures
were
important
due
to
Jackson's
requirement
of
biological
plausibility.
Their
surface
was
scanned
from
large
<a
href="/wiki/Maquette?qsrc=3044"
title="Maquette">maquettes</a>
before
numerous
digital
details
of
their
skeletons
and
muscles
were
added.
In
the
case
of
the
Balrog,
Gary
Horsfield
created
a
system
that
copied
recorded
imagery
of
fire.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Score">Score</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/Music_of_The_Lord_of_the_Rings_film_trilogy?qsrc=3044"
title="Music
of
The
Lord
of
the
Rings
film
trilogy">Music
of
The
Lord
of
the
Rings
film
trilogy</a>







</div>








<p>The
musical
score
for
the
<i>Lord
of
the
Rings</i>
films
was
composed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Howard_Shore?qsrc=3044"
title="Howard
Shore">Howard
Shore</a>.
It
was
performed
by
the
New
Zealand
Symphony
Orchestra,
The
London
Philharmonic
Orchestra,
The
London
Voices,
and
featured
several
vocal
soloists.
Two
original
songs,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/An%C3%ADron?qsrc=3044"
title="An&iacute;ron">An&iacute;ron</a>&quot;,
and
the
end
title
theme
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/May_It_Be?qsrc=3044"
title="May
It
Be">May
It
Be</a>&quot;,
were
composed
and
sung
by
<a
href="/wiki/Enya?qsrc=3044"
title="Enya">Enya</a>,
who
allowed
her
label,
<a
href="/wiki/Reprise_Records?qsrc=3044"
title="Reprise
Records">Reprise
Records</a>,
to
release
the
soundtrack
to
this
and
its
two
sequels.
In
addition
to
this,
Shore
composed
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/In_Dreams_(Howard_Shore_song)?qsrc=3044"
title="In
Dreams
(Howard
Shore
song)">In
Dreams</a>&quot;,
which
was
sung
by
Edward
Ross
of
the
London
Oratory
School
Schola.</p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Reception">Reception</span></h2>








<div
class="rellink
boilerplate
seealso">








See
also:









<a
href="/wiki/List_of_films_considered_the_best?qsrc=3044"
title="List
of
films
considered
the
best">List
of
films
considered
the
best</a>







</div>








<p><i>The
Lord
of
the
Rings:
The
Fellowship
of
the
Ring</i>
was
released
on
19
December
2001
in
3,359
cinemas
where
it
grossed
$47.2&nbsp;million
on
its
opening
weekend.
It
went
on
to
make
$314.7&nbsp;million
in
North
America
and
$555.9&nbsp;million
in
the
rest
of
the
world
for
a
worldwide
total
of
$870.7&nbsp;million.<sup
id="cite_ref-boxoffice_26-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-boxoffice-26"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p><i>The
Lord
of
the
Rings:
The
Fellowship
of
the
Ring</i>
received
mostly
positive
reviews
from
major
film
critics
and
was
one
of
the
best
reviewed
films
of
2001,
receiving
92%
positive
reviews
on
<a
href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes?qsrc=3044"
title="Rotten
Tomatoes">Rotten
Tomatoes</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-27"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert?qsrc=3044"
title="Roger
Ebert">Roger
Ebert</a>
gave
the
film
three
out
of
four
stars
and
wrote,
&quot;Peter
Jackson
...
has
made
a
work
for,
and
of,
our
times.
It
will
be
embraced,
I
suspect,
by
many
Tolkien
fans
and
take
on
aspects
of
a
cult.
It
is
a
candidate
for
many
Oscars.
It
is
an
awesome
production
in
its
daring
and
breadth,
and
there
are
small
touches
that
are
just
right&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Ebert_28-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Ebert-28"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/USA_Today?qsrc=3044"
title="USA
Today">USA
Today</a>
also
gave
the
film
three
out
of
four
stars
and
wrote,
&quot;this
movie
version
of
a
beloved
book
should
please
devotees
as
well
as
the
uninitiated&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Puig_29-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Puig-29"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
his
review
for
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times?qsrc=3044"
title="The
New
York
Times">The
New
York
Times</a></i>,
<a
href="/wiki/Elvis_Mitchell?qsrc=3044"
title="Elvis
Mitchell">Elvis
Mitchell</a>
wrote,
&quot;The
playful
spookiness
of
Mr.
Jackson's
direction
provides
a
lively,
light
touch,
a
gesture
that
doesn't
normally
come
to
mind
when
Tolkien's
name
is
mentioned&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Mitchell_30-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Mitchell-30"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i><a
href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly?qsrc=3044"
title="Entertainment
Weekly">Entertainment
Weekly</a></i>
magazine
gave
the
film
an
&quot;A&quot;
rating
and
Lisa
Schwarzbaum
wrote,
&quot;The
cast
take
to
their
roles
with
becoming
modesty,
certainly,
but
Jackson
also
makes
it
easy
for
them:
His
<i>Fellowship</i>
flows,
never
lingering
for
the
sake
of
admiring
its
own
beauty
...
Every
detail
of
which
engrossed
me.
I
may
have
never
turned
a
page
of
Tolkien,
but
I
know
enchantment
when
I
see
it&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Schwarzbaum_31-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Schwarzbaum-31"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
her
review
for
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Washington
Post">The
Washington
Post</a></i>,
Rita
Kempley
praised
the
cast,
in
particular,
&quot;Mortensen,
as
Strider,
is
a
revelation,
not
to
mention
downright
gorgeous.
And
McKellen,
carrying
the
burden
of
thousands
of
years'
worth
of
the
fight
against
evil,
is
positively
Merlinesque&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Kempley_32-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Kempley-32"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Time</i>
magazine's
Richard
Corliss
praised
Jackson's
work:
&quot;His
movie
achieves
what
the
best
fairy
tales
do:
the
creation
of
an
alternate
world,
plausible
and
persuasive,
where
the
young&nbsp;—
and
not
only
the
young&nbsp;—
can
lose
themselves.
And
perhaps,
in
identifying
with
the
little
Hobbit
that
could,
find
their
better
selves&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Corliss_33-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Corliss-33"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
his
review
for
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Village_Voice?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Village
Voice">The
Village
Voice</a></i>,
<a
href="/wiki/J._Hoberman?qsrc=3044"
title="J.
Hoberman">J.
Hoberman</a>
wrote,
&quot;Peter
Jackson's
adaptation
is
certainly
successful
on
its
own
terms&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Hoberman_34-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Hoberman-34"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a></i>
magazine's
<a
href="/wiki/Peter_Travers?qsrc=3044"
title="Peter
Travers">Peter
Travers</a>
wrote,
&quot;It's
emotion
that
makes
<i>Fellowship</i>
stick
hard
in
the
memory
...
Jackson
deserves
to
revel
in
his
success.
He's
made
a
three-hour
film
that
leaves
you
wanting
more&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Travers_35-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Travers-35"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup>
However,
in
his
review
for
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Guardian?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Guardian">The
Guardian</a></i>,
Peter
Bradshaw
wrote,
&quot;there
is
a
strange
paucity
of
plot
complication,
an
absence
of
anything
unfolding,
all
the
more
disconcerting
because
of
the
clotted
and
indigestible
mythic
back
story
that
we
have
to
wade
through
before
anything
happens
at
all.<sup
id="cite_ref-Bradshaw_36-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Bradshaw-36"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Awards">Awards</span></h2>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/List_of_accolades_received_by_The_Lord_of_the_Rings_film_trilogy?qsrc=3044"
title="List
of
accolades
received
by
The
Lord
of
the
Rings
film
trilogy">List
of
accolades
received
by
The
Lord
of
the
Rings
film
trilogy</a>







</div>








<p>In
2002,
the
film
won
four
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_Award?qsrc=3044"
title="Academy
Award">Academy
Awards</a>
out
of
thirteen
nominations.<sup
id="cite_ref-Oscars2002_37-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Oscars2002-37"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
winning
categories
were
for
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Cinematography?qsrc=3044"
title="Academy
Award
for
Best
Cinematography">Best
Cinematography</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Visual_Effects?qsrc=3044"
title="Academy
Award
for
Best
Visual
Effects">Best
Visual
Effects</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Makeup?qsrc=3044"
title="Academy
Award
for
Best
Makeup"
class="mw-redirect">Best
Makeup</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Score?qsrc=3044"
title="Academy
Award
for
Best
Original
Score">Best
Original
Score</a>.
Despite
its
praise
by
fans,
the
other
nominated
categories
of
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actor?qsrc=3044"
title="Academy
Award
for
Best
Supporting
Actor">Best
Actor
in
a
Supporting
Role</a>
(<a
href="/wiki/Ian_McKellen?qsrc=3044"
title="Ian
McKellen">Ian
McKellen</a>),
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Art_Direction?qsrc=3044"
title="Academy
Award
for
Best
Art
Direction"
class="mw-redirect">Best
Art
Direction</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Director?qsrc=3044"
title="Academy
Award
for
Best
Director">Best
Director</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Film_Editing?qsrc=3044"
title="Academy
Award
for
Best
Film
Editing">Best
Film
Editing</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song?qsrc=3044"
title="Academy
Award
for
Best
Original
Song">Best
Original
Song</a>
(<a
href="/wiki/Enya?qsrc=3044"
title="Enya">Enya</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Nicky_Ryan?qsrc=3044"
title="Nicky
Ryan">Nicky
Ryan</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Roma_Ryan?qsrc=3044"
title="Roma
Ryan">Roma
Ryan</a>
for
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/May_It_Be?qsrc=3044"
title="May
It
Be">May
It
Be</a>&quot;),
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Picture?qsrc=3044"
title="Academy
Award
for
Best
Picture">Best
Picture</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Sound?qsrc=3044"
title="Academy
Award
for
Best
Sound">Best
Sound</a>
(<a
href="/wiki/Christopher_Boyes?qsrc=3044"
title="Christopher
Boyes">Christopher
Boyes</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Michael_Semanick?qsrc=3044"
title="Michael
Semanick">Michael
Semanick</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Gethin_Creagh?qsrc=3044"
title="Gethin
Creagh">Gethin
Creagh</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Hammond_Peek?qsrc=3044"
title="Hammond
Peek">Hammond
Peek</a>),
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Costume_Design?qsrc=3044"
title="Academy
Award
for
Best
Costume
Design">Costume
Design</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Writing_(Adapted_Screenplay)?qsrc=3044"
title="Academy
Award
for
Best
Writing
(Adapted
Screenplay)">Best
Adapted
Screenplay</a>
were
not
won.</p>








<p>As
of
June
2010,
it
is
the
19th
highest-grossing
film
worldwide,
with
takings
of
US$870,761,744
from
worldwide
theatrical
box
office
receipts.<sup
id="cite_ref-BOM_0-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BOM-0"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
film
won
the
2002
<a
href="/wiki/Hugo_Award_for_Best_Dramatic_Presentation?qsrc=3044"
title="Hugo
Award
for
Best
Dramatic
Presentation">Hugo
Award
for
Best
Dramatic
Presentation</a>.
It
also
won
<i><a
href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)?qsrc=3044"
title="Empire
(film
magazine)">Empire</a></i>
readers'
Best
Film
award,
as
well
as
five
BAFTAs,
including
<a
href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Film?qsrc=3044"
title="BAFTA
Award
for
Best
Film">Best
Film</a>,
the
<a
href="/wiki/David_Lean?qsrc=3044"
title="David
Lean">David
Lean</a>
Award
for
Direction,
the
Audience
Award
(voted
for
by
the
public),
Best
Special
Effects,
and
Best
Make-up.
The
film
was
nominated
for
an
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Movie_Award_for_Best_Fight?qsrc=3044"
title="MTV
Movie
Award
for
Best
Fight">MTV
Movie
Award
for
Best
Fight</a>
between
Gandalf
and
Saruman.</p>








<p>In
June
2008,
AFI
revealed
its
&quot;Ten
top
Ten&quot;—the
best
ten
films
in
ten
&quot;classic&quot;
American
film
genres—after
polling
over
1,500
people
from
the
creative
community.
<i>The
Lord
of
the
Rings:
The
Fellowship
of
the
Ring</i>
was
acknowledged
as
the
second
best
film
in
the
fantasy
genre.<sup
id="cite_ref-38"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-39"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p><b><a
href="/wiki/American_Film_Institute?qsrc=3044"
title="American
Film
Institute">American
Film
Institute</a>
recognition</b></p>








<ul>









<li><a
href="/wiki/AFI%27s_100_Years...100_Heroes_and_Villains?qsrc=3044"
title="AFI's
100
Years...100
Heroes
and
Villains">AFI's
100
Years...100
Heroes
and
Villains</a>:










<ul>











<li>Gandalf
the
Grey
-
Nominated
Hero</li>










</ul>
</li>









<li><a
href="/wiki/AFI%27s_100_Years_of_Film_Scores?qsrc=3044"
title="AFI's
100
Years
of
Film
Scores">AFI's
100
Years
of
Film
Scores</a>
-
Nominated</li>









<li><a
href="/wiki/AFI%27s_100_Years...100_Cheers?qsrc=3044"
title="AFI's
100
Years...100
Cheers">AFI's
100
Years...100
Cheers</a>
-
Nominated</li>









<li><a
href="/wiki/AFI%27s_100_Years...100_Movies_(10th_Anniversary_Edition)?qsrc=3044"
title="AFI's
100
Years...100
Movies
(10th
Anniversary
Edition)">AFI's
100
Years...100
Movies
(10th
Anniversary
Edition)</a>
-
No.
50</li>









<li><a
href="/wiki/AFI%27s_10_Top_10?qsrc=3044"
title="AFI's
10
Top
10">AFI's
10
Top
10</a>
-
No.
2
Fantasy
film</li>








</ul>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Home_video">Home
video</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Theatrical_and_Extended_release">Theatrical
and
Extended
release</span></h3>








<p><i>The
Lord
of
the
Rings:
The
Fellowship
of
the
Ring</i>
was
released
on
VHS
and
DVD
on
6
August
2002.</p>








<p>A
few
months
later,
on
12
November
2002,
an
Extended
Edition
was
released
on
VHS
and
DVD,
with
30&nbsp;minutes
of
new
material,
added
special
effects
and
music,
plus
20&nbsp;minutes
of
fan-club
credits.
The
DVD
set
included
four
commentaries
and
over
three
hours
of
supplementary
material.</p>








<p>On
29
August
2006,
a
Limited
Edition
of
<i>The
Fellowship
of
the
Ring</i>
was
released
on
DVD.
The
set
included
both
the
Theatrical
and
Extended
editions
of
the
film
on
a
<a
href="/wiki/DVD?qsrc=3044#Capacity"
title="DVD">double-sided
disc</a>
along
with
all-new
bonus
material.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Blu-ray_edition">Blu-ray
edition</span></h3>








<p>The
theatrical
Blu-ray
version
of
<i>The
Lord
of
the
Rings</i>
was
released
in
the
United
States
on
6
April
2010.
There
were
two
separate
sets:
one
with
digital
copies
and
one
without.<sup
id="cite_ref-40"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
individual
Blu-ray
disc
of
<i>The
Fellowship
of
the
Ring</i>
was
released
on
14
September
2010
with
the
same
special
features
as
the
complete
trilogy
release,
except
there
was
no
digital
copy.<sup
id="cite_ref-41"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
Extended
Editions
for
Blu-ray
were
released
in
the
U.S.
on
28
June
2011.<sup
id="cite_ref-42"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<script
type="text/javascript">

(function()
{




$(document).ready(function(){
	
	
		$(".preview").click(function(e){	




		window.location
=
$(this).attr('value');	








});
		




	$(".preview").hover(function(e){	




		$('#preview').empty();




		$("#preview").append("<img
id='previewImg'
src='"+$(this).find('img').attr('src')+"'
alt='Smiley
face'
"+$(this).find('img').attr('value')+"='130'/>");	




		$("#preview")
				.css("display","block")




			.css("top",$(this).position().top
+
"px")




			.css("left",$(this).position().left
+
"px")
				.css("z-index","0")




			.fadeIn("fast");
			
			$("#previewAnc")
				.css("display","block")
				.css("top",($(this).position().top
-
1)
+
"px")




			.css("left",($(this).position().left
-
1)
+
"px")
				.css("z-index","1")




			.fadeIn("fast")
				.attr('onmousedown',
$(this).attr('onmousedown'))




			.attr('href',
$(this).attr('value'));








});
		
		$("#previewAnc").mouseout(function(){
			$('#preview')
				.css("display","none")
				.css("z-index","-1")
				.fadeIn("fast")
				.empty();
			$(this).css("display","none").css("z-index","-1");
		});
	
	});
})();

</script>

function
addEvent(obj,
evType,
fn)

{
	if(obj.addEventListener)

	{

		obj.addEventListener(evType,
fn,false);

		return
true;

	}

	else
if
(obj.attachEvent)

	{

		var
r
=
obj.attachEvent("on"+evType,
fn);

		return
r;

	}
	else
	{

		return
false;

	}

}
